Cache the template object\n        in render_context to avoid reparsing and loading when used in a for\n        loop.\n        \"\"\"\n        template = self.template.resolve(context)\n        # Does this quack like a Template?\n        if not callable(getattr(template, \"render\", None)):\n            # If not, try the cache and select_template().\n            template_name = template or ()\n            if isinstance(template_name, str):\n                template_name = (\n                    construct_relative_path(\n                        self.origin.template_name,\n                        template_name,\n                    ),\n                )\n            else:\n                template_name = tuple(template_name)\n            cache = context.render_context.dicts[0].setdefault(self, {})\n            template = cache.get(template_name)\n            if template is None:\n                template = context.template.engine.select_template(template_name)\n                cache[template_name] = template\n        # Use the base.Template of a backends.django.Template.\n        elif hasattr(template, \"template\"):\n            template = template.template\n        values = {\n            name: var.resolve(context) for name, var in self.extra_context.items()\n        }\n        if self.isolated_context:\n            return template.render(context.new(values))\n        with context.push(**values):\n            return template.render(context)\n\n\n@register.tag(\"block\")\ndef do_block(parser, token):\n    \"\"\"\n    Define a block that can be overridden by child templates.\n    \"\"\"\n    # token.split_contents() isn't useful here because this tag doesn't accept\n    # variable as arguments.\n    bits = token.contents.split()\n    if len(bits) != 2:\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\"'%s' tag takes only one argument\" % bits[0])\n    block_name = bits[1]\n    # Keep track of the names of BlockNodes found in this template, so we can\n    # check for duplication.\n    try:\n        if block_name in parser.__loaded_blocks:\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n                \"'%s' tag with name '%s' appears more than once\" % (bits[0], block_name)\n            )\n        parser.__loaded_blocks.append(block_name)\n    except AttributeError:  # parser.__loaded_blocks isn't a list yet\n        parser.__loaded_blocks = [block_name]\n    nodelist = parser.parse((\"endblock\",))\n\n    # This check is kept for backwards-compatibility. See #3100.\n    endblock = parser.next_token()\n    acceptable_endblocks = (\"endblock\", \"endblock %s\" % block_name)\n    if endblock.contents not in acceptable_endblocks:\n        parser.invalid_block_tag(endblock, \"endblock\", acceptable_endblocks)\n\n    return BlockNode(block_name, nodelist)\n\n\ndef construct_relative_path(\n    current_template_name,\n    relative_name,\n    allow_recursion=False,\n):\n    \"\"\"\n    Convert a relative path (starting with './' or '../') to the full template\n    name based on the current_template_name.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_name = relative_name.strip(\"'\\\"\")\n    if not new_name.startswith((\"./\", \"../\")):\n        # relative_name is a variable or a literal that doesn't contain a\n        # relative path.\n        return relative_name\n\n    if current_template_name is None:\n        # Unknown origin (e.g. Template('...').render(Context({...})).\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            f\"The relative path {relative_name} cannot be evaluated due to \"\n            \"an unknown template origin.\"\n        )\n\n    new_name = posixpath.normpath(\n        posixpath.join(\n            posixpath.dirname(current_template_name.lstrip(\"/\")),\n            new_name,\n        )\n    )\n    if new_name.startswith(\"../\"):\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            \"The relative path '%s' points outside the file hierarchy that \"\n            \"template '%s' is in.\" % (relative_name, current_template_name)\n        )\n    if not allow_recursion and current_template_name.lstrip(\"/\") == new_name:\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            \"The relative path '%s' was translated to template name '%s', the \"\n            \"same template in which the tag appears.\"\n            % (relative_name, current_template_name)\n        )\n    has_quotes = (\n        relative_name.startswith(('\"', \"'\")) and relative_name[0] == relative_name[-1]\n    )\n    return f'\"{new_name}\"' if has_quotes else new_name\n\n\n@register.tag(\"extends\")\ndef do_extends(parser, token):\n    \"\"\"\n    Signal that this template extends a parent template.\n\n    This tag may be used in two ways: ``{% extends \"base\" %}`` (with quotes)\n    uses the literal value \"base\" as the name of the parent template to extend,\n    or ``{% extends variable %}`` uses the value of ``variable`` as either the\n    name of the parent template to extend (if it evaluates to a string) or as\n    the parent template itself (if it evaluates to a construct_relative_path(parser.origin.template_name, bits[1])\n    parent_name = parser.compile_filter(bits[1])\n    nodelist = parser.parse()\n    if nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(ExtendsNode):\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            \"'%s' cannot appear more than once in the same template\" % bits[0]\n        )\n    return ExtendsNode(nodelist, parent_name)\n\n\n@register.tag(\"include\")\ndef do_include(parser, token):\n    \"\"\"\n    Load a template and render it with the current context. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JN8QrQmQ3mCvYdSaTzmJXE","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I understand the block inheritance system. Let me trace through the logic:\n\n1. When a template with `{% extends %}` is rendered, the `ExtendsNode.render()` method is called.\n2. It gets the parent template using `get_parent()`.\n3. It creates a `BlockContext` if one doesn't exist in `context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]`.\n4. It adds blocks from the current template to the block context using `block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)`.\n5. Then it checks if the parent template also has an extends tag. If it doesn't, it means the parent is the base template, so it adds the parent's blocks to the block context too.\n6. Finally, it renders the parent template.\n\nWhen a `BlockNode` is rendered:\n1. It checks if there's a `block_context` in the render context.\n2. If there is, it pops a block from the block context (FIFO order).\n3. If there's a block popped (meaning this block was overridden in a child template), it uses that block's nodelist.\n4. Otherwise, it uses its own nodelist.\n\nThe issue is likely in step 5 of `ExtendsNode.render()`. The code checks if the parent template has an extends tag, and if not (i.e., it's the base template), it adds the parent's blocks to the block context.\n\nHowever, when we have 3+ levels of inheritance, there's a problem:\n- Template A extends B (B extends C, C is base)\n- When A is rendered:\n  1. `block_context.add_blocks(A.blocks)` - adds A's blocks to the context\n  2. The parent is B (which also extends C)\n  3. Since B extends C, the code doesn't add B's blocks at this point\n  4. B is rendered\n\n- When B is rendered (as the parent of A):\n  1. `block_context.add_blocks(B.blocks)` - adds B's blocks\n  2. The parent is C (which doesn't extend anything)\n  3. Since C doesn't extend, it adds C's blocks\n  4. C is rendered\n\nThe FIFO queue ends up with blocks in the order [A.content, B.content, C.content].   The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n   105→    the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n   106→\n   107→    The decorator takes positional order.\n   110→\n   111→    Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n   112→    decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n   113→    use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n   114→\n   115→    Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n   116→\n   117→        def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n   118→            ...\n   119→\n   120→    to::\n   121→\n   122→        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n   123→        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n   124→            ...\n   125→\n   126→    After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n   127→\n   128→        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n   129→            ...\n   130→\n   131→    Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n   132→    parameters or change the remaining ones. This change will\n   144→    work without breaking existing code::\n   145→\n   146→        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n   147→        def some_func(request, *, new_param=None, option2=True, option1):\n   148→            ...\n   149→\n   150→    The @deprecate_posargs decorator adds a small amount of overhead. In most\n   151→    cases it won't be significant, but use with care in performance-critical\n   152→    code paths.\n   153→    \"\"\"\n   154→\n   155→    def decorator(func):\n   156→        if isinstance(func, type):\n   157→            raise TypeError(\n   158→                \"@deprecate_posargs cannot be applied to a class. (Apply it \"\n   159→                \"to the __init__ method.)\"\n   160→            )\n   161→        if isinstance(func, classmethod):\n   162→            raise TypeError(\"Apply @classmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n   163→        if isinstance(func, staticmethod):\n   164→            raise TypeError(\"Apply @staticmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n   165→\n   166→        params = inspect.signature(func).parameters\n   167→        num_by_kind = Counter(param.kind for param in params.values())\n   168→\n   169→        if num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.VAR_POSITIONAL] > 0:\n   170→            raise TypeError(\n   171→                \"@deprecate_posargs() cannot be used with variable positional `*args`.\"\n   172→            )\n   173→\n   174→        num_positional_params = (\n   175→            num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_ONLY]\n   176→            + num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_OR_KEYWORD]\n   177→        )\n   178→        num_keyword_only_params = num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY]\n   179→        if num_keyword_only_params < 1:\n   180→            raise TypeError(\n   181→                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires at least one keyword-only parameter \"\n   182→                \"(after a `*` entry in the parameters list).\"\n   183→            )\n   184→        if any(\n   185→            name not in params or params[name].kind != inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY\n   186→            for name in remappable_names\n   187→        ):\n   188→            raise TypeError(\n   189→                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires all remappable_names to be \"\n   190→                \"keyword-only parameters.\"\n   191→            )\n   192→\n   193→        num_remappable_args = len(remappable_names)\n   194→        max_positional_args = num_positional_params + num_remappable_args\n   195→\n   196→        func_name = func.__name__\n   197→        if func_name == \"__init__\":\n   198→            # - ClassName.__init__\n   202→            # - Nested.ClassName.__init__\n   203→            # - MyTests.test_case.<locals>.ClassName.__init__\n   204→            local_name = func.__qualname__.rsplit(\"<locals>.\", 1)[-1]\n   205→            class_name = local_name.replace(\".__init__\", \"\")\n   206→            func_name = class_name\n   207→\n   208→        def remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs):\n   209→            \"\"\"\n   210→            Move deprecated positional args to kwargs and issue a warning.\n   211→            Return updated (args, kwargs).\n   212→            \"\"\"\n   213→            if (num_positional_args := len(args)) > max_positional_args:\n   214→                raise TypeError(\n   215→                    f\"{func_name}() takes at most {max_positional_args} positional \"\n   216→                    f\"argument(s) (including {num_remappable_args} deprecated) but \"\n   217→                    f\"{num_positional_args} were given.\"\n   218→                )\n   219→\n   220→            # decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n    category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n    positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original positional order.\n\n    Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n    decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n    use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n\n    Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n\n        def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    to::\n\n        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n\n        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n    parameters or change the remaining ones. Edit your\"\n                \" MIDDLEWARE setting to insert\"\n                \" 'django.contrib.auth.middleware.AuthenticationMiddleware'\"\n                \" before the RemoteUserMiddleware class.\"\n            )\n        try:\n            username = request.META[self.header]\n        except KeyError:\n            # If specified header doesn't exist then remove any existing\n            # authenticated remote-user, or return (leaving request.user set to\n            # AnonymousUser by the AuthenticationMiddleware).\n            if self.force_logout_if_no_header and request.user.is_authenticated:\n                self._remove_invalid_user(request)\n            return\n        # If the user is already authenticated and that user is the user we are\n        # getting passed in the headers, then the correct user is already\n        # persisted in the session and we don't need to continue.\n        if request.user.is_authenticated:\n            if request.user.get_username() == self.clean_username(username, request):\n                return\n            else:\n                # An authenticated user is associated with the request, but\n                # it does not match the authorized user in the header.\n                self._remove_invalid_user(request)\n\n        # We are seeing this user for the first time in this session, attempt\n        # to authenticate the user.\n        user = auth.authenticate(request, remote_user=username)\n        if user:\n            # User is valid. Set request.user and persist user in the session\n            # by logging the user in.\n            request.user = user\n            auth.login(request, user)\n\n    async def __acall__(self, request):\n        await self.aprocess_request(request)\n        return await self.get_response(request)\n\n    async def aprocess_request(self, request):\n        # AuthenticationMiddleware is required so that request.user exists.\n        if not hasattr(request, \"user\"):\n            raise ImproperlyConfigured(\n                \"The Django remote user auth middleware requires the\"\n                \" authentication middleware to be installed. Edit your\"\n                \" MIDDLEWARE setting to insert\"\n                \" 'django.contrib.auth.middleware.AuthenticationMiddleware'\"\n                \" before the RemoteUserMiddleware class.\"\n            )\n        try:\n            username = request.META[\"HTTP_\" + self.header]\n        except KeyError:\n            # If specified header doesn't exist then remove any existing\n            # authenticated remote-user, or return (leaving request.user set to\n            # AnonymousUser by the AuthenticationMiddleware).\n            if self.force_logout_if_no_header:\n                user = await request.auser()\n                if user.is_authenticated:\n                    await self._aremove_invalid_user(request)\n            return\n        user = await request.auser()\n        # If the user is already authenticated and that user is the user we are\n        # getting passed in the headers, then the correct user is already\n        # persisted in the session and we don't need to continue.\n        if user.is_authenticated:\n            if user.get_username() == self.clean_username(username, request):\n                return\n            else:\n                # An authenticated user is associated with the request, but\n                # it does not match the authorized user in the header.\n                await self._aremove_invalid_user(request)\n\n        # We are seeing this user for the first time in this session, attempt\n        # to authenticate the user.\n        user = await auth.aauthenticate(request, remote_user=username)\n        if user:\n            # User is valid. Set request.user and persist user in the session\n            # by logging the user in.\n            request.user = user\n            await auth.alogin(request, user)\n\n    def clean_username(self, username, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Allow the backend to clean the username, if the backend defines a\n        clean_username method.\n        \"\"\"\n        backend_str = request.session[auth.BACKEND_SESSION_KEY]\n        backend = auth.load_backend(backend_str)\n        try:\n            username = backend.clean_username(username)\n        except AttributeError:  # Backend has no clean_username method.\n            pass\n        return username\n\n    def _remove_invalid_user(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Remove the current authenticated user in the request which is invalid\n        but only if the user is authenticated via the RemoteUserBackend.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            stored_backend = load_backend(\n                request.session.get(auth.BACKEND_SESSION_KEY, \"\")\n            )\n        except ImportError:\n            # backend failed to load\n            auth.logout(request)\n        else:\n            if isinstance(stored_backend, RemoteUserBackend):\n                auth.logout(request)\n\n    async def _aremove_invalid_user(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Remove the current authenticated user in the request which is invalid\n        but only if the user is authenticated via the RemoteUserBackend.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            stored_backend = load_backend(\n                await request.session.aget(auth.BACKEND_SESSION_KEY, \"\")\n            )\n        except ImportError:\n            # If the parent template doesn't extend anything, its blocks get added immediately. But when the parent itself extends another template, those blocks aren't added until the parent's ExtendsNode executes. This ordering could be problematic with nested inheritance chains, as blocks might be registered in the wrong sequence.\n\nTracing through a multi-level scenario: when page.html (which extends layout.html) renders, it initializes a BlockContext with page.html's blocks, then checks if layout.html has an ExtendsNode. Since base.html has no ExtendsNode, its blocks are added directly to the context, completing the inheritance chain.\n\nWhen rendering, the pop() operation retrieves blocks in LIFO order—base.html's outer block first, then layout.html's outer block for the 'outer' key, and base.html's inner block first, then layout.html's, then page.html's for the 'inner' key. Looking at the ExtendsNode.render() code again:\n\n```python\ndef render(self, context):\n    compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)\n\n    if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:\n        context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()\n    block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]\n\n    # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context\n    block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)\n\n    # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,\n    # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.\n    for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:\n        # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.\n        if not isinstance(node, TextNode):\n            if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):\n                blocks = {\n                    n.name: n\n                    for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)\n                }\n                block_context.add_blocks(blocks)\n            break\n\n    # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays\n    # the same.\n    with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):\n        return compiled_parent._render(context)\n```\n\nI notice that when the parent has an ExtendsNode, the parent's blocks aren't added to the block context immediately. The logic assumes the parent's ExtendsNode will handle this when rendered. But wait—the parent's ExtendsNode gets rendered after we call compiled_parent._render(), so the parent's blocks might not be available when they're needed. Actually, let me reconsider this flow more carefully.\n\nThe parent's ExtendsNode executes as part of compiled_parent._render(), which means it adds the blocks before they're actually used. Let me trace through the sequence step by step:\n\n1. page.html's ExtendsNode.render() is called\n   - block_context = BlockContext()\n   - block_context.add_blocks(page.blocks) = {'inner': page_inner}\n   - parent = layout.html (has ExtendsNode, so we don't add layout.blocks here)\n   - Call layout.html._render()\n\n2. Inside base.html._render():\n   - The template nodelist is processed\n   - base.html contains nodes like: \"{% block outer %}...\" \"{% endblock %}\"\n   - The outer block is rendered\n\nI see it now—when we render the outer block from base.html, we should use the one from layout.html, not base.html. When layout.html's outer block is rendered, it needs to find the inner block that was defined within it.\n\nWhen that inner block gets rendered, it pops from the block context and retrieves page.html's inner block instead.
